< Review>
Awesome food, and great service! We ordered the beer battered fish and chips, and the burger with bacon and grilled onions. Both were perfect.

The burger was so hot, that the juice burned my hand when I bit into it. Dining inside is available with plenty of distance between tables. Or, you can choose patio or sidewalk if you prefer to be outside. Masks must be worn unless you're sitting at your table.

If you go, ask for Nicole. She's awesome! üëå< /Review>

< review>
Local local favorite, they have all American fair and a decent beer selection. If you like sports and things like that it's great place to sneak in on Sunday as well. Obviously covered 19 is taking a toll on the ambiance because of indoor seating, however definitely a spot that is perfect to call in if you are a hotel-goer.

Simply give them a call, order some burgers and zucchini fries, and if they got wings get those too... Taking back to the hotel room and you can't go wrong.

And don't forget the truffle fries!</review>

<pictures>None</pictures><Name>Gabe Rodriguez</Name>< text>
Wine tastings end around 5pm in Napa. If you're like me, after a day of drinking, you'll find yourself wanting meat of some kind. For this reason, Norman Rose is a clutch choice.

It's called tavern for good reason. The decor plays this part well with wood framing the inside---has a rustic and classy feeling to it. At 5:30pm on a Saturday, we were sat right away with little wait. Being a smaller venue, I could imagine it getting busy easily though. Service was very good. Our waiter was fun, had great recommendations, and the food came out fast.

We were encouraged to try the ginger beer with the lamb burger or chicken sandwich. Having went with the staff favorite chicken sandwich, I was not disappointed! The ranch sauce is superb and worked really well with the chicken---contributing to it being consumed very fast (yum!). The truffle fries were also good, but restrain yourself. Eating too much of these can spoil the whole meal. Get a side of ranch to go with it.< /text>

106733997564731892352<//userid>
< Text>
Beer bar, plain and simple. I don't drink, but what I like about the place that it has major potential to be a jumping club for metal and punk music, original metal and pick music. Club is small and rectangular in space with the stage sitting far back of the club. Some sitting booths on the right with the bar in your immediate left when you enter.
It's gritty and Rae looking place. Reminds me of the old Vex or even CBGB's; that gritty. It has an old school charm that has potential to be long lasting club long after it's standing 5 year existence.
Sound was good, balanced and loud. The distinction of the instruments was only limited by the musicians stage volume. The equipment staging area is right next to the club outside. It's for the bands and people who smoke or just want to get outside for a bit. Get some fresh air you won't because that place is a big ole cloud of smoke. So, if you have any issues with that, be forewarned.
Overall I'd go there again and support this place. There are not that many metal clubs around and this one is right in the old neighborhood I use to request when younger. One of the places id least expect to find a metal club.</Text>
<user_name>Javier Marrufo< /user_name>< Pictures>

A bit grungy and dirty, but if you like the music on stage - punk, noise, out-jazz, plain 'ol weird stuff - you'll love the vibe and decor. Or lack thereof.

If you frequented Mr. T's Bowl in Highland Park in the 90s you'll notice that this has a similar vibe and has a lot of the same bands and people from that scene still hanging about. If you miss the old days when HLP wasn't all fancified, you'll love this little punk rock outpost in nearby Cypress Park. <Name>Ivan L< /Name><UserId.>118414269650201584973</UserId.><text>I tried liking stereo city based on the amount of good reviews on here. Before I begin I first called stereo city in Pomona for an alarm and the price seemed pretty high. Then I called san Bernardino and the price was much lower by a couple hundred bucks. The alarm install went great! So I went back for a remote start on my manual transmission vehicle and was quoted $200 over the phone.
I show up to make an appointment and they charge me $80 on top of the $200 "for taxes." Thought nothing of it until the following day.. that's a high tax rate!

Anyway I drop my vehicle off for an install that was supposedly taking 3 to 4 hours. It took 6. No biggie. By the time I recieved my vehicle and was handed the keys immediately I noticed my clutch pedal was way stiffer than when I returned it earlier in the day. So two days later I bring it back.

The techs supposedly checked and double checked and insisted I was a preexisting mechanical problem.  My vehicle doesn't have that many miles to have those kinds of clutch problems. RIGHT! So I drove off and a few weeks later driving all of a sudden when I shifted gears the clutch became smooth with a weird sound everytime I depressed the clutch pedal. (Look at picture provided)

In short what these professionals did was move my alarm unit in front of the large spring on my hydraulic clutch therefore hitting against it everytime I shifted gears creating the stiff clutch feeling. After so many times of it hitting against the alarm unit it finally moved. Don't worry stereo city I'll move these units myself.

Beware of these guys. Their installers could have used some mechanical common sense when doing these types of installs which could have resulted in a damaged alarm unit. Not to mention the unit was NOT placed in an inconspicuous area that a seasoned car thief wouldn't find.

I'd give 5 stars for customer service but for an incompetent install, and sketchy tax rate, and a failure to actually look at the mechanical problem by simply getting under the steering wheel and finding what the problem was I'd advise people to look elsewhere.

It is too bad I wanted to like stereo city.<//text>< pics>

<time>1480467716354</time><Rate>1</Rate><Text>I visited Stereo City at 596 South E Street in San Bernardino
to have my car's windows tinted. After I told the gentlemen
what car I had, he quoted me $160, then $173 after taxes. Why
so much? This is not an SUV but a sedan. I was told because it
has a lot of windows, so he justified the price. I agreed and
it got worked on.

Later that night, I approached a stop light and a car stopped
behind me. I then noticed in my rear view mirror that the
lower window was not tinted so the back window was not fully
complete.

I was totally apprehensive on going back there but I knew I
would not get treated fairly as a customer and/or get charged
additionally to get the lower back window completed.

After enough convincing from my wife, I went back and spoke to
the 1st person I saw. I told the young man I was not happy
with my tint job and would like it to be done completely.

The young man said I'll get someone to help you. He then
walked off as I sat down and patiently waited.

After an hour goes by, I walked to the counter and talked to
the 2nd person I saw. I said I talked to the 1st young man
about helping me and I've been waiting for an hour to be
helped. The 2nd person said I thought he helped you, Ok, I'll
help you.

The 2nd person seemed more compassionate to help me so I gave
him a chance and gave him my keys. He said there is a car
ahead of you and I will get you in in the next 30 minutes. I
agreed and went back over to the wait area and waited 30
minutes patiently.

After another 30 minutes go by, I walked to the 2nd man and
asked about the status of my vehicle. It was still parked and
no one brought it to the back of the shop.

At this point, I get very upset and the 3rd person steps and
the 2nd person walks away and sits at the register while
watching videos on his cell phone.

The 3rd person appears to be the manager and defends his team
outright. I told him the lower window was not tinted and I
expressed why would I be overcharged and the job not be
completely done.

I observed the back of the shop where all the cars are worked
on and noticed there is only one person working on the cars
while there are about five people standing and sitting around
up front.

The 4th person appears to be the owner and he defends the
manager outright. He wanted to get a calculator and try to
justify the price in front of me and I never felt so insulted
and disrespected.

I told him you do not have good customer service. He finally
said I was going to do it for you, but now you need to leave
my store. I got my keys and quietly left his store.

Next, I went to a professional tint shop outside of San
Bernardino, I was quoted $140 for every window on the car and
they said I made a mistake going there in the first place.
They even pointed out that my passenger front door has a gap in
the glass (tint work), so it did not fully cover the glass. He
also advised I get a refund or talk to the Better Business
Bureau.

As a business owner myself, if any of my Partners behaved in
such an unprofessional manner, which I've experienced, I would
employ a NEW team who are proud to be problem solvers and
provide excellent customer service.

This is the worst tint job and customer service I have ever
received. If you are reading this and you are someone who
expects excellent customer service, quality, and you work hard for
your dollar, I highly recommend doing business outside of San
Bernardino.
